Causality and Created Things
intermediate
10 min
The Mutakallim's Two Refutations of the Vacuum Argument
The mutakallim presents two arguments against the necessity of a vacuum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments the mutakallim uses to refute the philosopher's claim that a vacuum necessarily appears when two smooth surfaces are separated.

Core Idea
God creates air instantly or surfaces have pores: no vacuum needed.

In this passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif, the commentator presents the mutakallim's response to the famous vacuum argument. The philosopher argued that if two perfectly flat surfaces are in contact and one is lifted, a vacuum must form because air cannot move into the gap instantaneously. The mutakallim offers two counter-arguments: first, God can create air in the middle instantly; second, surfaces may consist of indivisible atoms with tiny air-filled pores, so when a atom rises, adjacent air immediately fills the space. Read the original Arabic and then work through the explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without stopping. Notice the structure: first the setting, then the two refutations marked by 'فإن عند المتكلم' and 'وأيضاً'.
The passage is dense but logical.
2
Identify the first refutation
The first refutation: God may create air instantly in the middle, so no transfer is needed. This relies on divine omnipotence.
3
Identify the second refutation
The second refutation: surfaces may be composed of atoms with pores. When an atom rises, air from neighboring pores fills the gap.
This avoids the need for air to move from edges.
4
Understand the force of these arguments
Both refutations show that a vacuum is not necessary. The mutakallim does not deny the possibility of a vacuum but shows it is not inevitable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد التاسع : المكان وهو من الكم المتصل بالأجزاء بالتدريج ويصل بالآخرة إلى الوسط فعند كونه على الأطراف يكون الوسط، خالياً عن الشاغل وهو المطلوب ( وهذا ) الوجه ( إلزامي ) مبني على ما هو مسلم ) عند الخصم لا برهاني مركب مما هو حق بحسب نفس الأمر، ( فإن عند المتكلم لا يجب انتقال الهواء إليه أي إلى الوسط من الأطراف ( بل قد يخلقه الله تعالى فيه دفعة ) فلا يلزم خلوه عن الشاغل أصلاً. وأيضاً يجوز عنده أن تكون الصفحة أجزاء لا تتجزأ بينها مسام صغيرة مملوءة بالهواء فينفذ إلى الوسط ذلك الهواء ويشغله . بل لا يكون هناك حينئذ شيء منقسم هو منطبق على مثله حتى يلزم خلوه بل المنطبق أجزاء لا تتجزأ متفاصلة على مثلها فإذا ارتفع واحد منها عن نظيره اتصل به الهواء المجاور له في المسام الضيقة جدا وأنت تعلم أنه إذا كان المقصود بهذا الوجه إلزام الحكماء فلا حاجة إلى ذلك التكلف في إثبات الصفحة الملساء، فإنهم معترفون بجوازها بل بوجودها أيضاً

قوله : ( فإن عند المتكلم ولا يمكن للحكيم أن يقول بخلقه بواسطة استعداد حصل بواسطة رفع إحدى الصفحتين، لأنَّ كل حادث مسبوق بمادة، والمادة لا تنفك عن الصورة، فلا بد من سبق جسم آخر بينهما، فلا تكونان متماستين هذا خلف

قوله : ( وأيضاً يجوز عنده إلخ) وما مر من أنه خلاف ما يشهد به البديهة، ففيه أنَّ البديهة إنما تحكم بالفرق بين الأجزاء المتفرقة والصفحة وهاهنا يعتبر الانفكاك بين أجزاء الصفحة دون المتفرقة، ويجوز أن يكون ذلك للفاعل المختار كما هو مذهب الأشاعرة أو للتأليف القائم بهما كما هو رأي أبي هاشم.

قوله : (بل بوجودها أيضاً ) فإنَّ سطوح الأجسام البسيطة كذلك عندهم.

قوله : (أي في آن) فسر الدفعة بذلك لأن جواز الارتفاع دفعة بمعنى ارتفاعها معاً لا يفيد لأنه يجوز أن يكون في زمان .

لا يجوز أن يكون بينهما صفحة رقيقة من الهواء فيتخلخل عند الرفع ؟ ولا يلزم التداخل لجواز التكاثف في أجزاء إحدى الصفحتين بل التكاثف لازم لأن سبب حركة الهواء من بينهما إلى الخارج هو الانطباق وانطباق الوسط مع انطباق الطرف وإلا لزم تفكك الأجزاء فيلزم التكاثف قلت : نفرض انطباق الصفحتين في صورة الاستدلال بأن يمر إحداهما من طرف الأخرى عليها إلى أن يتم الانطباق وادعاء تكاثف أجزاء صفحتي الحديد في هذه الصورة قريب من السفسطة، وكذا ادعاء انقلاب بعض أجزاء إحدى الصفحتين هواء متخلخلا بناء على جواز انقلاب الأجزاء الأرضية هواء، وإن لم يثبت وقوعه.
The second observation - the ninth purpose: place (al-makan) is from continuous quantity (al-kamm al-muttasil) by parts gradually and reaches ultimately to the middle; thus when it is on the edges, the middle becomes empty of the occupant, and that is what is sought. This is an obliging argument based on what is conceded by the opponent, not a demonstrative proof composed of what is true in itself. For according to the mutakallim, the transfer of air to it (i.e., to the middle) from the edges is not necessary; rather God most high may create it instantly therein, so its emptiness of the occupant does not necessarily follow. Also, according to him, it is possible that the surface consists of indivisible atoms (ajza' la tatajaza) between which there are small pores filled with air, so that air penetrates to the middle and occupies it. Then there would be no divided thing that is superimposed upon its like so that emptiness would be necessary; rather the superimposed are indivisible atoms separated upon their like, and when one of them rises from its counterpart, the adjacent air in the very narrow pores connects to it. And you know that if the purpose of this argument is to force the philosophers (al-hukama'), then there is no need for that effort in proving the smooth surface (al-safha al-malsa'), for they admit its possibility and indeed its existence. The comment on 'for according to the mutakallim': and the philosopher cannot say that He creates it by means of an aptitude produced by lifting one of the two surfaces, because every contingent event is preceded by matter, and matter is inseparable from form, so there must be another body between them; thus they are not contiguous, and this is a contradiction. The comment on 'and also it is possible according to him etc.': and what has passed that it contradicts what intuition testifies, the response is that intuition only judges the difference between scattered parts and the surface, and here the separation between parts of the surface is considered, not scattered parts, and that may be due to the free agent (al-fa'il al-mukhtar) as per the Ash'ari school, or due to the composition (al-ta'lif) inherent in them as per Abu Hashim's opinion. The comment on 'rather its existence also': for the surfaces of simple bodies are so according to them. The comment on 'i.e., in an instant': he explained 'instantaneous' (al-daf'a) by that because the permissibility of lifting 'daf'a' in the sense of their rising together does not suffice, for it may occur in time. There is no permissibility of a thin layer of air between them becoming rarefied upon lifting? And overlapping (al-tadakhul) is not necessary due to the permissibility of condensation (al-takathuf) in the parts of one of the two surfaces; rather condensation is necessary because the cause of the movement of air from between them to the outside is the superimposition (al-intibaq), and the superimposition of the middle with the superimposition of the edge, otherwise the parts would disintegrate, necessitating condensation. I say: we assume the superimposition of the two surfaces in the form of the inference by having one pass from the side of the other upon it until superimposition is complete, and claiming condensation of the parts of the two iron surfaces in this form is close to sophistry; likewise claiming the transformation of some parts of one of the two surfaces into rarefied air based on the permissibility of transformation of earthly parts into air, even if its occurrence has not been proven.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense by the mutakallim against the philosopher's argument that if two perfectly flat surfaces are in contact and one is lifted instantly, a vacuum would necessarily occur because air cannot move into the gap instantaneously. The mutakallim offers two refutations. First, God can create air in the middle instantly, negating the need for transfer. Second, surfaces may consist of indivisible atoms with tiny pores filled with air; when an atom rises, air from adjacent pores immediately fills the gap, so no vacuum occurs. The passage then discusses that the philosopher's own admission of smooth surfaces helps the mutakallim, because the philosopher already accepts such surfaces exist, so the argument's premise is conceded. The commentator clarifies that the philosopher cannot claim creation via aptitude because that would require matter. He also defends against the objection that the account contradicts intuition. The subsection ends with a discussion of condensation and rarefaction, rejecting the need for a thin air layer.

Key Terms
الرفع
الخلو
الفاعل المختار
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ
المسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallim denies all natural causality in this argument.
Correction: The mutakallim does not deny natural causality; he merely asserts that God's power can override it, and that the atomic structure provides a natural explanation as well.

Checkpoint
What are the two arguments given by the mutakallim against the necessity of a vacuum when lifting a flat surface?
A) Air is created instantly by God and surfaces have pores
B) Air is eternal and surfaces are smooth
C) Time is indivisible and motion is impossible
D) The philosopher admits the existence of vacuum

Key Takeaway
The mutakallim refutes the vacuum argument by appealing to divine omnipotence and atomic structure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God can create a solution instantly in your most hopeless situations, or do you rely solely on natural causes? How can you train your heart to expect divine intervention even when all physical possibilities seem exhausted?
?
The mutakallim's atomic theory reminds us that the physical world is not as continuous and predictable as it appears. When you plan your life, do you leave room for God's direct action at every moment, or do you act as if the world runs on fixed laws without His constant involvement?
?
If you were to truly internalize that every 'empty' space is filled by God's creative act, how would that change your anxiety about the future, especially in areas where you feel powerless and see no way forward?

Defending the Refutations: Further Clarifications
The commentator defends the mutakallim's refutations against objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subsequent discussion defending the mutakallim's refutations, including the philosophers' admission of smooth surfaces, the response to intuition, and the role of condensation and rarefaction.

Core Idea
The philosopher's own admissions and atomic theory bolster the mutakallim's case.

After presenting the two refutations, the commentator addresses potential objections and clarifies points. The philosophers already accept the possibility of smooth surfaces, so the argument's premise is conceded. The commentator also defends against the intuition that air cannot move through pores and discusses condensation and rarefaction. This lesson unpacks these additional defenses.

Guided Path
1
Read the remaining Arabic passage
Read from 'وأنت تعلم' to the end. Notice how the commentator defends each point.
This part is more dialectical.
2
Understand the point about smooth surfaces
The commentator notes that philosophers already admit the existence of smooth surfaces, so the mutakallim does not need to prove them.
3
Grasp the response to intuition
Intuition distinguishes between separated parts and a surface; here the separation is of atoms, not the whole surface.
This addresses an objection based on common sense.
4
Note the discussion on condensation
The commentator argues that condensation is necessary when air moves, and rejects the need for a thin air layer.
This reinforces the atomic theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد التاسع : المكان وهو من الكم المتصل بالأجزاء بالتدريج ويصل بالآخرة إلى الوسط فعند كونه على الأطراف يكون الوسط، خالياً عن الشاغل وهو المطلوب ( وهذا ) الوجه ( إلزامي ) مبني على ما هو مسلم ) عند الخصم لا برهاني مركب مما هو حق بحسب نفس الأمر، ( فإن عند المتكلم لا يجب انتقال الهواء إليه أي إلى الوسط من الأطراف ( بل قد يخلقه الله تعالى فيه دفعة ) فلا يلزم خلوه عن الشاغل أصلاً. وأيضاً يجوز عنده أن تكون الصفحة أجزاء لا تتجزأ بينها مسام صغيرة مملوءة بالهواء فينفذ إلى الوسط ذلك الهواء ويشغله . بل لا يكون هناك حينئذ شيء منقسم هو منطبق على مثله حتى يلزم خلوه بل المنطبق أجزاء لا تتجزأ متفاصلة على مثلها فإذا ارتفع واحد منها عن نظيره اتصل به الهواء المجاور له في المسام الضيقة جدا وأنت تعلم أنه إذا كان المقصود بهذا الوجه إلزام الحكماء فلا حاجة إلى ذلك التكلف في إثبات الصفحة الملساء، فإنهم معترفون بجوازها بل بوجودها أيضاً

قوله : ( فإن عند المتكلم ولا يمكن للحكيم أن يقول بخلقه بواسطة استعداد حصل بواسطة رفع إحدى الصفحتين، لأنَّ كل حادث مسبوق بمادة، والمادة لا تنفك عن الصورة، فلا بد من سبق جسم آخر بينهما، فلا تكونان متماستين هذا خلف

قوله : ( وأيضاً يجوز عنده إلخ) وما مر من أنه خلاف ما يشهد به البديهة، ففيه أنَّ البديهة إنما تحكم بالفرق بين الأجزاء المتفرقة والصفحة وهاهنا يعتبر الانفكاك بين أجزاء الصفحة دون المتفرقة، ويجوز أن يكون ذلك للفاعل المختار كما هو مذهب الأشاعرة أو للتأليف القائم بهما كما هو رأي أبي هاشم.

قوله : (بل بوجودها أيضاً ) فإنَّ سطوح الأجسام البسيطة كذلك عندهم.

قوله : (أي في آن) فسر الدفعة بذلك لأن جواز الارتفاع دفعة بمعنى ارتفاعها معاً لا يفيد لأنه يجوز أن يكون في زمان .

لا يجوز أن يكون بينهما صفحة رقيقة من الهواء فيتخلخل عند الرفع ؟ ولا يلزم التداخل لجواز التكاثف في أجزاء إحدى الصفحتين بل التكاثف لازم لأن سبب حركة الهواء من بينهما إلى الخارج هو الانطباق وانطباق الوسط مع انطباق الطرف وإلا لزم تفكك الأجزاء فيلزم التكاثف قلت : نفرض انطباق الصفحتين في صورة الاستدلال بأن يمر إحداهما من طرف الأخرى عليها إلى أن يتم الانطباق وادعاء تكاثف أجزاء صفحتي الحديد في هذه الصورة قريب من السفسطة، وكذا ادعاء انقلاب بعض أجزاء إحدى الصفحتين هواء متخلخلا بناء على جواز انقلاب الأجزاء الأرضية هواء، وإن لم يثبت وقوعه.
The second observation - the ninth purpose: place (al-makan) is from continuous quantity (al-kamm al-muttasil) by parts gradually and reaches ultimately to the middle; thus when it is on the edges, the middle becomes empty of the occupant, and that is what is sought. And you know that if the purpose of this argument is to force the philosophers (al-hukama'), then there is no need for that effort in proving the smooth surface (al-safha al-malsa'), for they admit its possibility and indeed its existence. The comment on 'i.e., in an instant': he explained 'instantaneous' (al-daf'a) by that because the permissibility of lifting 'daf'a' in the sense of their rising together does not suffice, for it may occur in time. There is no permissibility of a thin layer of air between them becoming rarefied upon lifting? Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense by the mutakallim against the philosopher's argument that if two perfectly flat surfaces are in contact and one is lifted instantly, a vacuum would necessarily occur because air cannot move into the gap instantaneously. The mutakallim offers two refutations. First, God can create air in the middle instantly, negating the need for transfer. Causality and Created Things
advanced

The Philosopher's Objection: Lifting Is a Gradual Movement
Philosopher's objection and mutakallim's initial response on lifting and time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the philosopher argues that lifting a surface is a movement requiring time, and how the mutakallim initially responds by asserting the simultaneity of air movement.

Core Idea
Lifting a surface is a gradual movement, not an instantaneous event.

The philosopher challenges the mutakallim's claim that air can fill a gap instantly when two surfaces separate. He argues that separation itself is a movement over a distance, which necessarily takes time. This short passage presents the core objection and the mutakallim's first line of defense.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of movement
The philosopher defines lifting as movement in the sense of traversal (qat'), not instantaneous change. Recognize that all movement over a distance requires time.
This is a key distinction in kalam: movement as gradual vs. instantaneous.
2
Follow the philosopher's reasoning
Since lifting traverses a divisible distance, it must occur in divisible time. Therefore, lifting cannot be instantaneous. This is the core of the objection.
The divisibility of time and space is assumed.
3
See the mutakallim's counter
The mutakallim responds that the time of lifting is exactly the time air moves from the edge to the middle. So no vacuum occurs during lifting.
This is a claim of temporal simultaneity, not denial of gradual movement.
4
Address the non-contact objection
An objector says that when the surfaces separate, non-contact (lamumasa) occurs instantaneously, and at that instant air cannot have moved, so vacuum would exist. The mutakallim replies that non-contact itself occurs after some time, not at the very start.
This answer is brief here; it will be expanded in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن الارتفاع حركة يريد أنَّ حركة الارتفاع حركة بمعنى القطع، لا حركة بمعنى

عنده في زمان ) إذ لا بد أن تكون الحركة على مسافة منقسمة وقطع بعضها مقدم على قطع جميعها فلا يتصور وقوع الحركة في آن بل في زمان ) وأنه ( أي الزمان ( منقسم إلى غير النهاية أي لا ينتهي في الانقسام إلى حد يقف عنده ( ففي زمان ارتفاعها يسلك الهواء من طرفها إلى الوسط ) فلا يلزم خلوه لا يقال : لا إذا رفعنا الصفحة حصل اللامماسة التي هي آنية عندهم ويلزم الخلو لأنَّ الحركة تدريجية فيصح الإلزام لأنا نقول : اللامماسة وإن كانت آنية كالمماسة إلا أنها لا تحصل إلا بعد

قوله : ( فإن الارتفاع حركة قال الشارح قُدس سره في حواشي شرح المطالع توضيح هذا المنع أنه إذا فرض زوال الانطباق على أي وجه يمكن أن يتصور فيه كانت العليا مرتفعة عن السافلة بينهما . إما أن يكون منقسماً في جهة الارتفاع أو لا والثاني محال وإلا لم يكن فاصلاً فتعين الأول فيكون مسافة بتجزئه لا يمكن قطعها إلا بحركة في زمان . فظهر أن الارتفاع لا يكون دفعياً.

قوله: (ففي زمان (ارتفاعها فإن الانطباق مبدأ حركة الارتفاع وحركة السلوك وزمان الحركتين واحد وإن كان حركة الارتفاع متقدمة بالذات على حركة السلوك فالارتفاع والوصول إلى الوسط كلاهما زمانيان بمعنى أنهما حاصلان في أي آن يفرض في زمان تينك الحركتين ولا يتعين حصولهما في آن معين وكما أن قطع الهواء لأجزاء المسافة الصفحة الذي يحصل به الوصول إلى الوسط تدريجي كذلك قطع الصفحة لأجزاء المسافة الذي يحصل به الارتفاع تدريجي بلا تفاوت فتدبر فإنه مما زل فيه الأقدام وعرض دون فهمه الأوهام . قوله : (لا يقال الخ) يعني أنَّ الإلزام المذكور إنما لا يتم إذا لم يتعرض في اللامماسة واكتفى بأن الارتفاع دفعي أما لو تعرض لها وقيل : إذا رفعنا الصفحة حصل اللامماسة فهي متأخرة عن الرفع وإلا لكانت حاصلة حال المماسة فيجتمع المتقابلان وهي آنية فلا يمكن حصول حركة السلوك في ذلك الآن فتكون متأخرة عنها لامتناع السلوك حال المماسة للزوم التداخل فيكون الوسط في آن اللامماسة خالياً عن الهواء ليتم الإلزام. قوله : (لأنا نقول إلخ) حاصله أنَّ السلوك ليس متأخراً عن اللامماسة لأنها وإن كانت آنية التوسط وحاصل كلامه أنَّ حركة الارتفاع واقعة على مسافة منقسمة، وكذلك حركة الهواء من الطرف إلى الوسط، وقطع إحدى المسافتين مع قطع الأخرى زماناً، وإن كان حركة الارتفاع متقدمة بالذات على الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط، وليس تقدمها بالزمان حتى يرد عليه أنَّ الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط تكون على مسافة منقسمة فقطع النصف الأول مقدم على قطع النصف الآخر ففي زمان قطع النصف الأول يكون الوسط خاليا بالضرورة هكذا قيل : وفيه نظر لأنا سلمنا اتحاد القطعين المذكورين زماناً . لكن نقول زمان السلوك إلى الوسط إن كان عين زمان السلوك إلى الطرف لم ينطبق الزمان على الحركة المنطبقة على المسافة وإن كان بعده وإن لطف فقد خلا الوسط ولا يخفى أن هذا لا يندفع بادعاء اتحاد حركتي الارتفاع زماناً، فتأمل.
The comment on 'for the lifting is a movement': He intends that the movement of lifting is movement in the sense of traversal (qat'), not movement in the sense of [instantaneous change]. According to him, it occurs in time, since movement must be over a divisible distance, and the traversal of some of it is prior to the traversal of all of it; thus it is inconceivable for movement to occur in an instant, but rather in time. And that time is divisible infinitely, i.e., it does not terminate in division at a limit where it stops. So in the time of its lifting, the air travels from its side to the middle, so its emptiness does not necessarily follow. It cannot be said: no, when we lift the surface, non-contact (al-lamumasa) occurs, which is instantaneous according to them, and emptiness follows because movement is gradual, so the objection stands. For we say: non-contact, even if it is instantaneous like contact, does not occur except after [some time]. The comment on 'for the lifting is a movement': The commentator (sharh) said in his glosses on Sharh al-Matali' clarifying this prevention: If the removal of superimposition (al-intibaq) is assumed in any conceivable manner, the upper is raised above the lower with a gap between them. Either that gap is divisible in the direction of height or not; the second is impossible, otherwise it would not be a separator, so the first is determined, and it is a distance that, due to its divisibility, cannot be traversed except by a movement in time. Thus it is clear that lifting cannot be instantaneous. The comment on 'so in the time of its lifting': For superimposition is the starting point of the lifting movement and the movement of circulation, and the time of the two movements is one, even if the lifting movement is ontologically prior to the circulation movement. So lifting and reaching the middle are both temporal, in the sense that they occur in any instant assumed in the time of those two movements, and they are not determined to occur at a specific instant. And just as the traversal of the air of the parts of the distance of the surface, by which reaching the middle is achieved, is gradual, so too the traversal of the surface of the parts of the distance, by which lifting is achieved, is gradual without difference. So reflect, for it is something in which feet have slipped and minds have failed to comprehend. The comment on 'it cannot be said, etc.': That is, the aforementioned objection is not established only if one does not address non-contact and is satisfied that lifting is instantaneous. But if one addresses it and says: when we lift the surface, non-contact occurs, and it is subsequent to the lifting, otherwise it would have existed during contact, and two opposites would coincide, and it is instantaneous, so the movement of circulation cannot occur in that instant, so it would be subsequent to it, because circulation during contact is impossible due to the necessity of overlapping. Thus the middle would be empty of air in the instant of non-contact, so the objection is established. The comment on 'for we say, etc.': Its summary is that circulation is not subsequent to non-contact, because even if it is instantaneous, the middle [is not empty]. And the summary of his speech is that the lifting movement occurs over a divisible distance, likewise the movement of air from the side to the middle, and the traversal of one of the two distances together with the traversal of the other is temporal, even if the lifting movement is ontologically prior to the movement from the side to the middle. It is not temporally prior such that it could be objected that the movement from the side to the middle is over a divisible distance, so the traversal of the first half is prior to the traversal of the other half; so during the time of the first half's traversal, the middle is necessarily empty. Thus it is said: and in it there is consideration, because we admitted the simultaneity of the two traversals in time. But we say: the time of circulation to the middle, if it is the same as the time of circulation to the side, then the time does not correspond to the movement superimposed on the distance; and if it is after it, even if slightly, then the middle has become empty. And it is not hidden that this is not repelled by claiming the simultaneity of the two lifting movements in time. So reflect.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the philosopher's stringent objection: lifting a surface is a movement that requires time because it traverses a divisible distance; instantaneous lifting is impossible. Therefore, the mutakallim cannot avoid vacuum by claiming instantaneous air creation, because the lifting itself takes time, and during that time air must travel from edges to middle. The mutakallim counters by asserting that the time of lifting and the time of air circulation are simultaneous: both movements are gradual and occur over the same time interval. Even if lifting is temporally prior in essence, it is not temporally prior in a way that creates a vacuum interval. The commentator expands with an argument from Sharh al-Matali' showing that if the surfaces separate, the gap must be divisible, so movement is necessary and instantaneous lifting impossible. Then he handles a further objection: when the surfaces just separate, non-contact occurs instantaneously, and at that instant air cannot have moved, so vacuum must exist. The answer is that non-contact itself is not instantaneous in the sense of occurring without any time; it occurs after some temporal interval. The summary of the mutakallim's final position is that the two movements are ontologically but not temporally sequential, so the middle is never empty.

الزمان
القطع
اللامماسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the mutakallim denies that lifting is a gradual movement.
Correction: The mutakallim accepts gradual lifting but asserts that air movement is simultaneous, not sequential.

Checkpoint
Why does the philosopher argue that lifting cannot be instantaneous?
A) Because lifting involves a change in quality
B) Because lifting traverses a divisible distance
C) Because the mutakallim says so
D) Because vacuum is impossible

Key Takeaway
The philosopher's objection relies on the gradual nature of lifting; the mutakallim's defense is that air movement is temporally simultaneous with lifting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a moment when you felt a sudden change in your heart—repentance, faith, or clarity. After this lesson, do you believe that change was truly instantaneous, or did it require a process over time? How might that shape your patience with yourself when growth feels slow?
?
The philosopher feared an empty gap; the mutakallim insisted no moment is devoid of filling. In your spiritual life, which 'gaps' do you worry about—times when you feel distant from Allah, or moments of doubt? What 'air' fills those gaps, and how can you trust that Allah has not left you empty even then?
?
If every movement, even the lifting of a surface, involves time and divine control, how does that change your view of your smallest actions? Will you stop taking any moment for granted, knowing that each fraction of time is filled with Allah's creation and command?

Causality and Created Things
advanced
8 min
Clarifying the Simultaneity of Movements and the Non-Contact Objection
Commentator's expansion of the mutakallim's response, addressing the non-contact objection in detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the commentator's detailed argument that both lifting and air movement are gradual and simultaneous, and how the non-contact objection is fully resolved.

Core Idea
Both lifting and air movement are gradual and share the same time, so no vacuum occurs at any instant.

The commentator expands the mutakallim's response with a rigorous argument from Sharh al-Matali'. He shows that if the surfaces separate, the gap must be divisible, so lifting is necessarily gradual. He then addresses a subtle objection about the instantaneous moment of separation, demonstrating that non-contact itself occurs after a temporal interval, not at a true instant. This lesson completes the picture of the mutakallim's position on vacuum.

Guided Path
1
Follow the commentator's preliminary argument
Read the Sharh al-Matali' argument that the gap between surfaces must be divisible, so lifting requires time. This reinforces the gradual nature of lifting.
This is a response to an attempt to make lifting instantaneous.
2
Understand the simultaneity claim
The commentator states that the time of lifting and the time of air circulation are one, even if lifting is ontologically prior. This means they occur in the same temporal interval.
Ontological priority does not imply temporal priority.
3
Address the non-contact objection in detail
The objector says that when the surfaces just separate, non-contact is instantaneous and at that instant the middle is empty. The commentator replies that non-contact is not truly instantaneous; it occurs after a temporal duration, however small.
This reply depends on denying that any part of movement occurs in a true instant.
4
Reflect on the final nuance
The commentator notes a potential subtle issue: if we admit temporal simultaneity, but if the time of circulation to the middle is identical to time of circulation to the side, then the time does not match the movement. But this is a technical point left for reflection.
This shows the depth of the debate and the need for careful reasoning.

قوله : ( فإن الارتفاع حركة يريد أنَّ حركة الارتفاع حركة بمعنى القطع، لا حركة بمعنى

عنده في زمان ) إذ لا بد أن تكون الحركة على مسافة منقسمة وقطع بعضها مقدم على قطع جميعها فلا يتصور وقوع الحركة في آن بل في زمان ) وأنه ( أي الزمان ( منقسم إلى غير النهاية أي لا ينتهي في الانقسام إلى حد يقف عنده ( ففي زمان ارتفاعها يسلك الهواء من طرفها إلى الوسط ) فلا يلزم خلوه لا يقال : لا إذا رفعنا الصفحة حصل اللامماسة التي هي آنية عندهم ويلزم الخلو لأنَّ الحركة تدريجية فيصح الإلزام لأنا نقول : اللامماسة وإن كانت آنية كالمماسة إلا أنها لا تحصل إلا بعد

قوله : ( فإن الارتفاع حركة قال الشارح قُدس سره في حواشي شرح المطالع توضيح هذا المنع أنه إذا فرض زوال الانطباق على أي وجه يمكن أن يتصور فيه كانت العليا مرتفعة عن السافلة بينهما . إما أن يكون منقسماً في جهة الارتفاع أو لا والثاني محال وإلا لم يكن فاصلاً فتعين الأول فيكون مسافة بتجزئه لا يمكن قطعها إلا بحركة في زمان . فظهر أن الارتفاع لا يكون دفعياً.

قوله: (ففي زمان (ارتفاعها فإن الانطباق مبدأ حركة الارتفاع وحركة السلوك وزمان الحركتين واحد وإن كان حركة الارتفاع متقدمة بالذات على حركة السلوك فالارتفاع والوصول إلى الوسط كلاهما زمانيان بمعنى أنهما حاصلان في أي آن يفرض في زمان تينك الحركتين ولا يتعين حصولهما في آن معين وكما أن قطع الهواء لأجزاء المسافة الصفحة الذي يحصل به الوصول إلى الوسط تدريجي كذلك قطع الصفحة لأجزاء المسافة الذي يحصل به الارتفاع تدريجي بلا تفاوت فتدبر فإنه مما زل فيه الأقدام وعرض دون فهمه الأوهام . قوله : (لا يقال الخ) يعني أنَّ الإلزام المذكور إنما لا يتم إذا لم يتعرض في اللامماسة واكتفى بأن الارتفاع دفعي أما لو تعرض لها وقيل : إذا رفعنا الصفحة حصل اللامماسة فهي متأخرة عن الرفع وإلا لكانت حاصلة حال المماسة فيجتمع المتقابلان وهي آنية فلا يمكن حصول حركة السلوك في ذلك الآن فتكون متأخرة عنها لامتناع السلوك حال المماسة للزوم التداخل فيكون الوسط في آن اللامماسة خالياً عن الهواء ليتم الإلزام. قوله : (لأنا نقول إلخ) حاصله أنَّ السلوك ليس متأخراً عن اللامماسة لأنها وإن كانت آنية التوسط وحاصل كلامه أنَّ حركة الارتفاع واقعة على مسافة منقسمة، وكذلك حركة الهواء من الطرف إلى الوسط، وقطع إحدى المسافتين مع قطع الأخرى زماناً، وإن كان حركة الارتفاع متقدمة بالذات على الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط، وليس تقدمها بالزمان حتى يرد عليه أنَّ الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط تكون على مسافة منقسمة فقطع النصف الأول مقدم على قطع النصف الآخر ففي زمان قطع النصف الأول يكون الوسط خاليا بالضرورة هكذا قيل : وفيه نظر لأنا سلمنا اتحاد القطعين المذكورين زماناً . لكن نقول زمان السلوك إلى الوسط إن كان عين زمان السلوك إلى الطرف لم ينطبق الزمان على الحركة المنطبقة على المسافة وإن كان بعده وإن لطف فقد خلا الوسط ولا يخفى أن هذا لا يندفع بادعاء اتحاد حركتي الارتفاع زماناً، فتأمل.

Commentary
This passage presents the philosopher's stringent objection: lifting a surface is a movement that requires time because it traverses a divisible distance; instantaneous lifting is impossible. ?

Causality and Created Things

The Regress Argument for the Possibility of Void
Presents the regress argument for the necessity of void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that if there were no void, any small motion would cause all bodies to move, leading to collision.

Core Idea
Even a gnat's movement would shake the whole world if there were no void.

This lesson presents the second proof for the possibility of void, which relies on the absurd consequences of denying void. The argument shows that a small motion in a plenum leads to an infinite regress of transfers, forcing all bodies to move. We will trace the logical steps of this regress and see why it refutes the denial of void.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional statement
The proof begins with a conditional: if there were no void, then all bodies would collide and move. Read this carefully to set up the argument.
The consequent is claimed to be necessarily false.
2
Understand the circularity (dawr)
The explanation shows that a moving body cannot transfer to an occupied place without the occupant moving, but the occupant cannot move unless the first body moves, creating a circular dependency.
This circularity forces the analysis to a third body.
3
Follow the infinite regress (tasalsul)
Since each transfer depends on another, the reasoning continues to a fourth body, then a fifth, and so on infinitely. No body remains stationary.
This regress is the core of the proof.
4
Appreciate the conclusion: universal collision
The regress implies that all bodies in the world must move, which is absurd because it would mean constant collision. Therefore, the assumption that there is no void is false.
The proof demonstrates the necessity of void to avoid this absurdity.

الثاني من الوجهين الدالين على جواز الخلاء أنه لولا وجود الخلاء فيما بين الأجسام تصادمت أجسام العالم بأسرها وتحركت بحركة بقة مثلاً وإن كانت تلك الحركة قليلة جداً واللازم باطل بالضرورة بيان الشرطية أن الجسم المتحرك كالبقة ينتقل من مكانه بحركته إلى مكان آخر والفرض أنه أي ذلك المكان الآخر مملوء بجسم آخر إذ المفروض أن لا خلاء فيما بين الأجسام وهو أعني ذلك الجسم الآخر ينتقل من مكانه البتة إذ لا يتداخل جسمان ضرورة ولا ينتقل الجسم الآخر إلى مكان الجسم الأول لأن انتقاله إليه مشروط بانتقال الأول عنه لئلا يلزم تداخلهما وانتقاله عنه أي انتقال الأول عن مكانه مشروط بانتقال هذا الجسم عن مكانه إليه أي إلى مكان الأول ليخلو مكانه عنه فيمكن انتقال الأول إليه فيدور لأن كل واحد من الانتقالين مشروط بالآخر وموقوف عليه فهو أي الجسم الآخر إذن ينتقل إلى مكان جسم آخر مغاير للأولين والكلام فيه أي في هذا الجسم الثالث كما في الأول السابق عليه وهو الجسم الثاني إذ لا بد أن ينتقل الثالث عن مكانه حتى يتصور انتقال الثاني إليه ولا يجوز أن ينتقل الثالث إلى مكان الثاني ولا إلى مكان الأول لاستلزامه الدور كما عرفت بل إلى مكان جسم رابع فننقل الكلام إليه ويتسلسل فتتحرك أجسام العالم كلها وهذا الوجه الثاني أيضاً إلزامي مبني على قواعد الحكماء فإن عند المتكلمين على تقدير كون العالم مملوءاً قد يعدم الله الجسم الذي قدامه أي قدام الجسم المتحرك حال انتقاله بحركته إلى مكانه فيملؤه المتحرك ويخلق جسماً آخر في مكانه أي مكان المتحرك ليملأ مكانه فلا يلزم الخلاء ولا تصادم الأجسام ولا يتم هذا الإلزام على الحكماء إلا بإبطال التخلخل والتكاثف وإلا جاز أن يتخلخل ما خلفه أي يزيد مقدار ما خلف المتحرك من الأجسام فيملأ مكانه بمقداره الزائد من غير أن ينتقل ما خلفه عن مكانه ويتكاثف ما قدامه أي ينتقص مقدار ما قدامه من الأجسام فيخلي له مكاناً من غير أن ينتقل عن مكانه وبهذا القدر يندفع الإلزام إلا أنه زاد في البيان فقال : إلى غاية ما يطيع ما خلفه أو ما قدامه لذلك التخلخل أو التكاثف بحسب قوة الحركة وضعفها وتصويره أن المتحرك في الهواء يدفع الهواء
The second of the two proofs indicating the possibility of void: that if there were no void between bodies, all the bodies of the world would collide and move, for example, with the movement of a gnat, even if that movement were very small. The consequent is necessarily false. The explanation of the conditional: the moving body, like the gnat, transfers from its place by its motion to another place. The assumption is that that other place is filled with another body, since it is assumed that there is no void between bodies. That body, I mean that other body, transfers from its place absolutely, since two bodies cannot interpenetrate necessarily. Nor does the other body transfer to the place of the first body, because its transfer to it is conditioned upon the first body's having transferred from it to avoid interpenetration. And its transfer from it, i.e., the first body's transfer from its place, is conditioned upon this body's transfer from its place to it, i.e., to the place of the first, so that its place becomes empty of it, and thus the first can transfer to it. So there is a circularity (dawr), because each of the two transfers is conditioned upon the other and dependent upon it. So that other body then transfers to the place of another body different from the first two. And the discussion concerning it, i.e., concerning this third body, is as in the first preceding it, which is the second body. Because it is necessary for the third body to transfer from its place so that the second's transfer to it can be conceived. Nor is it permissible for the third to transfer to the place of the second, nor to the place of the first, because that would entail the circularity as you have known. Rather, it transfers to the place of a fourth body, and we transfer the discussion to it, and so on infinitely (tasalsul). Thus all the bodies of the world move. And this second proof is also a dialectical argument based on the principles of the philosophers. For according to the theologians, on the assumption that the world is filled, God may annihilate the body in front of it, i.e., in front of the moving body at the moment of its transfer by its motion to its place, and the moving body fills it, and He creates another body in its place, i.e., the place of the moving body, to fill its place, so no void occurs and no collision of bodies. But this dialectical argument is not valid against the philosophers unless rarefaction and condensation are invalidated. Otherwise, it would be permissible for what is behind it to rarefy, i.e., the volume of the bodies behind the moving body increases, and thus fills its place by its increased volume without what is behind it transferring from its place, and for what is in front of it to condense, i.e., the volume of the bodies in front of it decreases, thus vacating a place for it without transferring from its place. To this extent the argument is repelled. But he added in the explanation, saying: 'to the utmost limit that what is behind or in front of it obeys that rarefaction or condensation according to the strength and weakness of the motion.' And its description is that the moving body in the air pushes the air.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a complete proof for the possibility of void, presented as the second of two arguments. The author begins by stating the conditional: if there were no void, all bodies would collide and move. He then explains why. A moving body must occupy a new place, but if that place is already occupied (since no void), the occupant must move. This leads to a circular dependency: the first body cannot move unless the second moves out, and the second cannot move unless the first moves out. The author resolves this by positing a third body, but then an infinite regress follows: each transfer depends on another, and since no body can remain stationary, all bodies must move. This is absurd (collision of all bodies). The author then notes that this argument is dialectical (ilzami) against the philosophers, because theologians can avoid it by invoking divine power to annihilate and create bodies. However, the argument still holds against the philosophers unless they reject rarefaction and condensation, which could allow bodies to change volume without linear displacement. The author adds a further detail: the extent of rarefaction/condensation depends on the force of motion. Finally, he illustrates with a description of a moving body pushing air. The lesson carefully follows the logical structure: conditional statement, explanation of the regress, conclusion of absurdity, dialectical nature, and the rebuttal regarding rarefaction/condensation.

تصادم
تسلسل
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would happen if a gnat moves in a world with no void?
A) Only the gnat moves.
B) All bodies would have to move, leading to collision.
C) The gnat cannot move at all.
D) The gnat creates a void by its motion.

Key Takeaway
The denial of void leads to the absurd conclusion that any motion forces all bodies to move, proving that void must exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the movement of a gnat would necessitate the movement of all bodies without void, what does your smallest sin require to be atoned for? Are you aware that nothing is insignificant in the sight of Allah?
?
The argument shows that denying 'empty space' leads to absurdity. In your spiritual life, do you fill every moment with distraction, afraid of the 'void' of silence and reflection? What chaos does that avoidance cause?
?
Are you caught in a regress of excuses—each reason for delaying repentance depending on another? What would it take for you to break the cycle and submit to the clear proof that void (and thus tawheed) must be acknowledged?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
Dialectical Qualification and the Role of Rarefaction and Condensation
Explains the dialectical nature of the proof and the counterarguments from occasionalism and rarefaction/condensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the second proof is dialectical and how the philosophers could avoid it by appealing to rarefaction and condensation.

Core Idea
The proof only works against philosophers who deny occasionalism and rarefaction/condensation.

The previous lesson presented the regress argument for the possibility of void. However, the author notes that this argument is dialectical (ilzami) because it relies on principles that not all schools accept. Specifically, theologians can avoid it by invoking divine action, while philosophers can appeal to rarefaction and condensation. This lesson unpacks the dialectical nature and the conditions under which the proof holds.

Guided Path
1
Understand what 'ilzami' means
A dialectical argument is one that is valid only given the opponent's premises. Here, the proof is built on the philosophers' principles, not on universal truths.
The author explicitly says it is 'mabniyy 'ala qawa'id al-hukama'.
2
See how theologians escape
Theologians (mutakallimun) can avoid the regress by positing that God annihilates the body in front and creates a new body behind, so no collision occurs and no void is needed.
This relies on occasionalism—direct divine intervention.
3
Understand rarefaction/condensation as a potential escape for philosophers
Philosophers who reject occasionalism can still avoid the regress if they allow bodies to change volume (rarefaction and condensation) without moving linearly. Then the rear body can expand to fill the vacated space, and the front body can contract to create space.
The author adds that the extent of rarefaction/condensation depends on the strength of the motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a complete proof for the possibility of void, presented as the second of two arguments. The lesson carefully follows the logical structure: conditional statement, explanation of the regress, conclusion of absurdity, dialectical nature, and the rebuttal regarding rarefaction/condensation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second proof is a self-evident proof accepted by all.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the proof is dialectical (ilzami) and only valid against those who accept the philosophers' premises and reject occasionalism and rarefaction/condensation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This proof works only against those who reject both occasionalism and rarefaction/condensation. Are there beliefs you hold that you have never tested against alternative worldviews? Will you commit today to honestly confronting the assumptions behind your own convictions?

Causality and Created Things

Collision and the Necessary Chain of Bodies
Definition of collision and its necessary consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of collision (ṣadm) and how the absence of void leads to a necessary chain of pushes among bodies.

Core Idea
Absence of void forces all bodies into mutual pushing.

In this first part of the commentary on the second proof, the author explains the key term 'collision' and shows that if no void exists, bodies must push each other in a chain. This establishes the foundation for the proof's argument against atomism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the definition of collision
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the definition of ṣadm (pushing) and taṣādum (mutual pushing).
The commentator defines these terms explicitly.
2
Trace the logical chain from no void to mutual pushing
Follow the reasoning: if no void exists, a push cannot dissipate into empty space, so it must continue through bodies until it reaches the end. This creates a chain of pushes.
Notice the phrase 'from the other side' — the push reaches the opposite extreme.
3
Understand why the chain stops at interpenetration
The chain continues until the impossibility of interpenetration prevents further motion. This is the point where the sequence ends.
The commentator uses 'ilā an yantafī' (until it ceases) to mark the termination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ( تصادمت إلخ ) الصدم الدفع والتصادم التدافع فاللازم عن عدم الخلاء تدافع أجسام العالم كلها لأنه إذا انتهى الدفع إلى منتهى الطرف الآخر ولا يندفع ذلك لعدم المكان فيدفع ما بعده ثم، وثم إلى آخر الأجسام وهكذا إلى أن ينتفي لامتناع التداخل فمعنى قوله: ويتسلسل أنه يلزم عدم انقطاع حركات الأجسام . قوله: ففي ذلك الزمان يتحرك الجسم من الطرف إلى الوسط فلا إلزام فيه بحث لأن المسافة التي يتحقق فيها حركة الجسم إنما تتحقق في أن اللامماسة فما لم يحصل اللامماسة لم يتصور الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط وإلا لزم التداخل والحركة الزمانية لا تتحقق في ذلك الآن بل بعده زماناً فيخلو الوسط في ذلك الزمان فإن قلت: كل لا مماسة تفرض فهي مسبوقة بلا مماسة أخرى لا إلى نهاية ولا يوجد لا مماسة الأولى حتى يقال: الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط متأخرة عنها واقعة في زمان يكون آن تلك اللامماسة مبدأ ذلك الزمان فيلزم الخلو قلت: يكفي في إثبات المطلوب أنَّ العقل يجزم إجمالاً بأنه ما لم يحصل اللامماسة لم يتصور الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط وإن لم يمكن أن يشير إلى لامماسة معينة بأنها متقدمة على تلك الحركة. قوله: (فتتحرك أجسام العالم كلها حمل التسلسل على المعنى اللغوي وجعل اللازم حركة جميع الأجسام فالتصادم على هذا دفع الأجسام بعضها بعضاً وقد عرفت ما هو الحقيق بالقبول . قوله: ( إلى غاية إلخ) متعلق بيتخلخل ويتكاثف بتضمين معنى التدافع كما بينه الشارح قدس سره . الجسم الثاني السابق عليه حمل الكلام على المتبادر من السياق. وإلا فلا مانع من رجوعه إلى الثاني وحمل الأول على ظاهره كل ذلك ظاهر بأدنى تأمل . قوله: ( ولا يجوز أن ينتقل الثالث إلى مكان الثاني لاستلزامه الدور. وأيضاً مكان الثاني مشغول بالأول كما هو المفروض فلا يعقل انتقال الثالث إليه لاستلزامه التداخل. قوله: ( ويتسلسل فتتحرك أجسام العالم كلها التسلسل هاهنا على معناه اللغوي فلا ينافي تناهي المواد ثم المحال هاهنا حركة المحال هاهنا حركة جميع الأجسام بحركة بقة على أن فيه المطلوب لأن حركة المجموع أيضاً يقتضي أن يكون للأخير مكان خال والتحقيق أنَّ المحال امتناع حركة بقة لتوقفها على الأخرى المتوقفة عليها بالآخرة وأنه دور محال كما ذكره الشارح المقاصد ولو جعل الكلام إلزامياً ويجعل المحال لزوم حركة الأفلاك حركة أينية مع عدم قبولها إياها عندهم لم يبعد . قوله: ( وتصويره أنَّ المتحرك في الهواء) المفهوم من هذا التصوير التكاثف، إنما يتحقق في واحد مما قدام المتحرك وهو المنتهي وكذا التخلخل إنما يوجد في واحد مما بعده وهو المنتهى والأقرب إلى العقول وهو المتبادر من عبارة المتن أن يكون ما قدام المتحرك يدفع ما
His saying: 'they would collide (tasādamat), etc.' — collision (ṣadm) is pushing, and mutual collision (taṣādum) is mutual pushing. So the necessary consequence of the absence of void is mutual pushing of all bodies of the world, because when the push reaches the extreme of the other side and it does not push back due to lack of space, it pushes what is after it, and then, and then, until the end of bodies, and so on until it ceases due to the impossibility of interpenetration. So the meaning of his saying 'and it goes on infinitely' is that the motions of bodies necessarily do not cease. His saying: 'so in that time the body moves from the edge to the middle, so there is no obligation' — there is an investigation in it, because the distance in which the motion of the body occurs is only realized in the state of non-contact (lā-mumāssa). So as long as non-contact has not occurred, motion from the edge to the middle is inconceivable; otherwise interpenetration would be necessary. And temporal motion does not occur at that instant, but after it temporally, so the middle becomes empty at that time. If you say: every non-contact that is assumed is preceded by another non-contact infinitely, and there is no first non-contact such that it can be said: the motion from the edge to the middle is posterior to it, occurring in a time whose beginning is that instant of non-contact, so emptiness follows — I say: it suffices for proving the required that the intellect judges in summary that motion from the edge to the middle is inconceivable as long as non-contact has not occurred, even if one cannot point to a specific non-contact as being prior to that motion. His saying: 'so all the bodies of the world move' — he took 'tasalsul' in its linguistic sense and made the necessary consequence the motion of all bodies. So collision (taṣādum) in this sense is the pushing of bodies against each other. And you have known what is deserving of acceptance. His saying: 'to the utmost limit (ilā ghāya), etc.' — it is connected to 'rarefy and condense' with the implication of mutual pushing, as the commentator, may his secret be sanctified, explained. 'The second body preceding it' — he interpreted the speech according to the apparent meaning of the context. Otherwise, there is no obstacle to referring it to the second and taking the first in its apparent sense. All that is obvious with minimal reflection. His saying: 'nor is it permissible for the third to transfer to the place of the second because it would entail circularity (dawr). Also, the place of the second is occupied by the first, as assumed, so it is not reasonable for the third to transfer to it because that would entail interpenetration.' His saying: 'and it goes on infinitely (tasalsul), so all the bodies of the world move' — 'tasalsul' here is in its linguistic sense, so it does not contradict the finitude of materials. Then the absurdity here is the motion of all bodies by the motion of a gnat, such that the required is in it because the motion of the whole also requires that the last have an empty place. And the verification is that the absurdity is the impossibility of the motion of the gnat because it depends on the other, which in turn depends on it in the end, and that is an impossible circularity (dawr) as the author of al-Maqāṣid mentioned. And if one makes the speech dialectical and makes the absurdity the necessary occurrence of the motion of the spheres as a local motion despite their not admitting it according to them, it would not be far. His saying: 'and its description is that the moving body in the air' — what is understood from this description is condensation (takāthuf). It occurs only in one of the bodies in front of the moving body, which is the end point. Similarly, rarefaction (takhalkhul) occurs only in one of the bodies behind it, which is the end point. And the closest to minds and the apparent from the text's expression is that what is in front of the moving body pushes what...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the second proof. It begins by explaining the meaning of 'collision' (ṣadm) as pushing and mutual pushing. The commentator clarifies that if no void exists, bodies would push each other in a chain until it stops at the end, due to the impossibility of interpenetration. Next, the commentator addresses an objection about temporal motion from the edge to the middle. He argues that motion requires a state of non-contact (lā-mumāssa) before the motion, so the middle becomes empty temporally. A question is raised about an infinite regress of non-contacts, but the answer is that the intellect judges summarily that motion is impossible without a state of non-contact, even if the specific instant cannot be pinpointed. The commentary then discusses the phrase 'so all the bodies of the world move', explaining that 'tasalsul' is used linguistically and the consequent is mutual pushing. The commentator then elaborates on the phrase 'to the utmost limit' linking it to rarefaction and condensation with the sense of mutual pushing. He clarifies the referent of 'the second body preceding it' and affirms multiple plausible interpretations. Next, he explains why the third body cannot move to the second's place: circularity and the second's place being occupied by the first. He reiterates that 'tasalsul' is linguistic and does not conflict with finite matter; the real absurdity is the motion of all bodies from a gnat's motion, which entails a circular dependence. Alternatively, if taken dialectically, the absurdity could be the motion of the spheres. Finally, the commentator interprets the description of the moving body in the air as illustrating condensation at the front and rarefaction at the back, each occurring at the extreme end. The lesson thus clarifies each key point of the original proof, responding to potential objections and refining terminology.

تصادم
تداخل

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why does the chain of pushes come to an end?
A) Because there is no more space for pushing.
B) Because the last body refuses to move.
C) Because interpenetration is impossible.
D) Because the push becomes too weak.

Key Takeaway
The absence of void necessitates mutual pushing of bodies in a chain that terminates at interpenetration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that bodies cannot sustain motion without a stopping point. Where in your life do you see a chain of events that feels endless, yet must end with Allah’s decree? How does this change how you view that struggle?
?
The impossibility of interpenetration forces the chain to stop. What does this teach you about Allah’s control over even the most fundamental physical laws? Will you trust Him to stop the chains of hardship in your life at the right moment?
?
If every push in the universe is connected until interpenetration, reflect on how your actions are linked to others. Are you pushing others toward goodness or away from it, knowing that the chain ends with Allah’s permission? What will you change today?

Temporal Motion and the Problem of Non-Contact
Dialectical exchange on temporal motion and non-contact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection regarding temporal motion and the commentator's response that the intellect judges motion requires a state of non-contact.

Core Idea
Motion from edge to middle is inconceivable without a prior state of non-contact.

In this section, the commentator addresses a potential objection: if the body moves from the edge to the middle in time, then the middle must become empty. But what about the infinite regress of non-contacts? The answer is that the intellect's summary judgment suffices, even if a specific instant cannot be pinpointed.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection about temporal motion
Read the passage carefully. The objector argues that motion from the edge to the middle requires a non-contact (lā-mumāssa) before the motion, and that non-contact leads to an infinite regress.
The objection is presented as 'فإن قلت...' (if you say...).
2
Understand the commentator's reasoning about non-contact
The commentator explains that motion over a distance requires the bodies to be separate (non-contact). Without that separation, motion would require interpenetration, which is impossible.
The key phrase: 'فما لم يحصل اللامماسة لم يتصور الحركة' — 'as long as non-contact has not occurred, motion is inconceivable.'
3
Reflect on the answer regarding intellectual judgment
The commentator answers the infinite regress objection by stating that the intellect's summary judgment is sufficient: we know that motion requires prior non-contact, even if we cannot identify the exact instant of that non-contact.
The answer starts with 'قلت: يكفي في إثبات المطلوب أنَّ العقل يجزم إجمالاً' — 'I say: it suffices for proving the required that the intellect judges in summary.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ( تصادمت إلخ ) الصدم الدفع والتصادم التدافع فاللازم عن عدم الخلاء تدافع أجسام العالم كلها لأنه إذا انتهى الدفع إلى منتهى الطرف الآخر ولا يندفع ذلك لعدم المكان فيدفع ما بعده ثم، وثم إلى آخر الأجسام وهكذا إلى أن ينتفي لامتناع التداخل فمعنى قوله: ويتسلسل أنه يلزم عدم انقطاع حركات الأجسام . قوله: ففي ذلك الزمان يتحرك الجسم من الطرف إلى الوسط فلا إلزام فيه بحث لأن المسافة التي يتحقق فيها حركة الجسم إنما تتحقق في أن اللامماسة فما لم يحصل اللامماسة لم يتصور الحركة من الطرف إلى الوسط وإلا لزم التداخل والحركة الزمانية لا تتحقق في ذلك الآن بل بعده زماناً فيخلو الوسط في ذلك الزمان فإن قلت: كلها حمل التسلسل على المعنى اللغوي وجعل اللازم حركة جميع الأجسام فالتصادم على هذا دفع الأجسام بعضها بعضاً وقد عرفت ما هو الحقيق بالقبول . قوله: ( إلى غاية إلخ) متعلق بيتخلخل ويتكاثف بتضمين معنى التدافع كما بينه الشارح قدس سره . الجسم الثاني السابق عليه حمل الكلام على المتبادر من السياق. وإلا فلا مانع من رجوعه إلى الثاني وحمل الأول على ظاهره كل ذلك ظاهر بأدنى تأمل . قوله: ( ولا يجوز أن ينتقل الثالث إلى مكان الثاني لاستلزامه الدور. وأيضاً مكان الثاني مشغول بالأول كما هو المفروض فلا يعقل انتقال الثالث إليه لاستلزامه التداخل. قوله: ( ويتسلسل فتتحرك أجسام العالم كلها التسلسل هاهنا على معناه اللغوي فلا ينافي تناهي المواد ثم المحال هاهنا حركة المحال هاهنا حركة جميع الأجسام بحركة بقة على أن فيه المطلوب لأن حركة المجموع أيضاً يقتضي أن يكون للأخير مكان خال والتحقيق أنَّ المحال امتناع حركة بقة لتوقفها على الأخرى المتوقفة عليها بالآخرة وأنه دور محال كما ذكره الشارح المقاصد ولو جعل الكلام إلزامياً ويجعل المحال لزوم حركة الأفلاك حركة أينية مع عدم قبولها إياها عندهم لم يبعد . قوله: ( وتصويره المتن أن يكون ما قدام المتحرك يدفع ما
His saying: 'they would collide (tasādamat), etc.' — collision (ṣadm) is pushing, and mutual collision (taṣādum) is mutual pushing. So the necessary consequence of the absence of void is mutual pushing of all bodies of the world, because when the push reaches the extreme of the other side and it does not push back due to lack of space, it pushes what is after it, and then, and then, until the end of bodies, and so on until it ceases due to the impossibility of interpenetration. So the meaning of his saying 'and it goes on infinitely' is that the motions of bodies necessarily do not cease. His saying: 'so in that time the body moves from the edge to the middle, so there is no obligation' — there is an investigation in it, because the distance in which the motion of the body occurs is only realized in the state of non-contact (lā-mumāssa). So as long as non-contact has not occurred, motion from the edge to the middle is inconceivable; otherwise interpenetration would be necessary. Linguistic Tasalsul and the Absurdity of Universal Motion
Clarification of tasalsul and its consequences including gnat example and motion in air.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator interprets 'tasalsul' linguistically to avoid an infinite regress of matter, and how he explains the absurdity of universal motion and the process of rarefaction/condensation.

Core Idea
'Tasalsul' here means a continuous sequence, not an infinite material chain.

The latter part of the commentary deals with the consequences of the second proof. The author clarifies that the 'tasalsul' mentioned is linguistic and does not conflict with finite matter. He then explains the absurdity of moving all bodies by a gnat's motion, and finally describes how motion in air involves condensation in front and rarefaction behind.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic sense of tasalsul
Read the passage where the commentator specifies that 'tasalsul' here is used in its linguistic sense, not implying an infinite chain of material substances.
Key phrase: 'التسلسل هاهنا على معناه اللغوي فلا ينافي تناهي المواد'
2
Analyze the gnat example and circular dependence
The commentator presents an example: the motion of a gnat supposedly moves all bodies. This leads to a circular dependence (dawr) because each motion depends on another, making motion impossible.
The absurdity is that the gnat's motion cannot happen without prior motions, which depend on it.
3
Examine the description of motion in air
The final part describes how a body moving in air causes condensation at the front extreme and rarefaction at the back extreme. This illustrates the process of mutual pushing.
The text says: 'التكاثف، إنما يتحقق في واحد مما قدام المتحرك وهو المنتهي' — 'condensation occurs only in one of the bodies in front of the moving body, which is the end point.'

His saying: 'and it goes on infinitely (tasalsul), so all the bodies of the world move' — 'tasalsul' here is in its linguistic sense, so it does not contradict the finitude of materials. Then the absurdity here is the motion of all bodies by the motion of a gnat, such that the required is in it because the motion of the whole also requires that the last have an empty place. And the verification is that the absurdity is the impossibility of the motion of the gnat because it depends on the other, which in turn depends on it in the end, and that is an impossible circularity (dawr) as the author of al-Maqāṣid mentioned. And if one makes the speech dialectical and makes the absurdity the necessary occurrence of the motion of the spheres as a local motion despite their not admitting it according to them, it would not be far. His saying: 'and its description is that the moving body in the air' — what is understood from this description is condensation (takāthuf). It occurs only in one of the bodies in front of the moving body, which is the end point. Similarly, rarefaction (takhalkhul) occurs only in one of the bodies behind it, which is the end point. And the closest to minds and the apparent from the text's expression is that what is in front of the moving body pushes what...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the second proof. It begins by explaining the meaning of 'collision' (ṣadm) as pushing and mutual pushing. The commentator clarifies that if no void exists, bodies would push each other in a chain until it stops at the end, due to the impossibility of interpenetration. Next, the commentator addresses an objection about temporal motion from the edge to the middle. He argues that motion requires a state of non-contact (lā-mumāssa) before the motion, so the middle becomes empty temporally. A question is raised about an infinite regress of non-contacts, but the answer is that the intellect judges summarily that motion is impossible without a state of non-contact, even if the specific instant cannot be pinpointed. The commentary then discusses the phrase 'so all the bodies of the world move', explaining that 'tasalsul' is used linguistically and the consequent is mutual pushing. The commentator then elaborates on the phrase 'to the utmost limit' linking it to rarefaction and condensation with the sense of mutual pushing. He clarifies the referent of 'the second body preceding it' and affirms multiple plausible interpretations. Next, he explains why the third body cannot move to the second's place: circularity and the second's place being occupied by the first. He reiterates that 'tasalsul' is linguistic and does not conflict with finite matter; the real absurdity is the motion of all bodies from a gnat's motion, which entails a circular dependence. Alternatively, if taken dialectically, the absurdity could be the motion of the spheres. Finally, the commentator interprets the description of the moving body in the air as illustrating condensation at the front and rarefaction at the back, each occurring at the extreme end. The lesson thus clarifies each key point of the original proof, responding to potential objections and refining terminology.

دور
تخلخل
تكاثف
غاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tasalsul always implies an infinite regress of material causes.
Correction: Here it is used linguistically to mean a continuous sequence without implying infinity of matter, as stated: 'التسلسل هاهنا على معناه اللغوي فلا ينافي تناهي المواد'.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'tasalsul' mean in this context?
A) An infinite chain of material bodies.
B) A linguistic sense of continuous sequence.
C) A logical fallacy.
D) The motion of the spheres.

Key Takeaway
‘Tasalsul’ here is linguistic, and the supposed motion of all bodies by a gnat leads to an impossible circular dependence.

The scholars rejected a seemingly plausible chain because it led to contradiction. Is there an area of your life—like your habits, your excuses, or your relationships—where you accept a chain of reasoning that ends in contradiction? What will you do about it this week?
?

The Second Ilzam Argument and the Mutakallimun's Response
Presents the ilzam argument and the mutakallimun's response using annihilation and creation, then the need to refute takhalkhul and takathuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' second ilzam argument regarding motion in a plenum and how the mutakallimun respond, including the role of rarefaction and condensation.

Core Idea
Motion in a plenum forces a choice between void, infinite regress, or divine intervention — and rarefaction offers a natural way out.

The philosophers argue that if the world is full, any motion would lead to infinite regress or void. The mutakallimun counter that God can intervene by annihilation and creation, but the real challenge is for the philosophers to refute rarefaction and condensation, which can explain motion without void. This passage unpacks that dialectic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation without analyzing. Let the argument's flow come through.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the ilzam argument
Find the philosophers' argument: if a body moves in a plenum, the third body must move to a fourth's place, leading to infinite regress of motion.
Look for 'أن ينتقل الثالث عن مكانه' and 'ويتسلسل'.
3
Understand the mutakallimun's direct response
Notice that they invoke God's power to annihilate the front body and create a new one behind, avoiding void and collision.
This is the 'إعدام' and 'خلق' solution.
4
Recognize the key condition
The author states the obligation is only effective if rarefaction (takhalkhul) and condensation (takathuf) are invalidated. This shifts the burden to the philosophers.
The phrase 'إلا بإبطال التخلخل والتكاثف' is crucial.
5
Analyze the example of air motion
Study the illustration: pushing air in front and attracting air behind leads to rarefaction and condensation, allowing motion without void. Note how strength of motion affects distance.
This shows rarefaction/condensation as a natural explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن ينتقل الثالث عن مكانه حتى يتصور انتقال الثاني إليه ولا يجوز أن ينتقل الثالث إلى مكان الثاني ولا إلى مكان الأول لاستلزامه الدور كما عرفت بل إلى مكان جسم رابع فننقل الكلام إليه ويتسلسل فتتحرك أجسام العالم كلها وهذا الوجه الثاني أيضاً إلزامي مبني على قواعد الحكماء فإن عند المتكلمين على تقدير كون العالم مملوءاً قد يعدم الله الجسم الذي قدامه أي قدام الجسم المتحرك حال انتقاله بحركته إلى مكانه فيملؤه المتحرك ويخلق جسماً آخر في مكانه أي مكان المتحرك ليملأ مكانه فلا يلزم الخلاء ولا تصادم الأجسام ولا يتم هذا الإلزام على الحكماء إلا بإبطال التخلخل والتكاثف وإلا جاز أن يتخلخل ما خلفه أي يزيد مقدار ما خلف المتحرك من الأجسام فيملأ مكانه بمقداره الزائد من غير أن ينتقل ما خلفه عن مكانه ويتكاثف ما قدامه أي ينتقص مقدار ما قدامه من الأجسام فيخلي له مكاناً من غير أن ينتقل عن مكانه وبهذا القدر يندفع الإلزام إلا أنه زاد في البيان فقال إلى غاية ما يطيع ما خلفه أو ما قدامه لذلك التخلخل أو التكاثف بحسب قوة الحركة وضعفها وتصويره أنَّ المتحرك في الهواء يدفع الهواء الذي قدامه ويدفع ذلك الهواء هواء آخر وهكذا لكن هذا الدفع يتفاوت ويضعف إلى أن ينتهي إلى هواء لا ينقاد للدفع لضعف الدافع فهذا الدافع المتوسط بين ما دفعه لم يندفع به يضطر إلى قبول حجم أصغر مما كان وكذا ما خلف هذا المتحرك من الهواء ينجذب إليه ما يقرب منه وينجذب إلى هذا المنجذب ما يليه وهكذا ويضعف الانجذاب حتى ينتهي إلى ما لا ينجذب فيضطر المتوسط إلى قبول حجم أكبر ولا شك أنَّ الدفع والانجذاب المذكورين يتفاوتان بحسب قوة الحركة وضعفها فإذا كانت الحركة قوية امتدا في مسافة كثيرة وإن كانت ضعيفة كانا مسافة قليلة
That the third body should move from its place so that the second's movement to it can be conceived, and it is not allowed for the third to move to the second's place nor to the first's place because it necessitates circularity as you know, but rather to the place of a fourth body, so we transfer the discussion to it, and it would regress infinitely, so all bodies of the world would move. And this second aspect is also an obligation based on the principles of the philosophers. For according to the mutakallimun, on the assumption that the world is full, God may annihilate the body in front of it, i.e., in front of the moving body at the moment of its movement to its place, so the mover fills it, and He creates another body in its place, i.e., the place of the mover, to fill its place, so no void and no collision of bodies occur. And this obligation is not completed against the philosophers except by invalidating rarefaction and condensation. Otherwise, it would be possible for what is behind it to rarely, i.e., the amount of the bodies behind the mover increases, so they fill its place by that increased amount without what is behind moving from its place, and for what is in front of it to condense, i.e., the amount of the bodies in front of it decreases, so they vacate a place for it without moving from its place. And to this extent the obligation is repelled. But he added in the explanation, saying: 'To the limit that what is behind it or what is in front of it obeys that rarefaction or condensation according to the strength and weakness of the motion.' And its illustration is that a mover in air pushes the air in front of it, and that air pushes another air, and so on. But this pushing varies and weakens until it reaches air that does not yield to pushing due to the weakness of the pusher. So this intermediate pusher between what it pushed – it did not push it – is compelled to accept a smaller size than it had. Similarly, the air behind this mover is attracted to it, what is near it, and to this attracted one what follows it, and so on, and the attraction weakens until it reaches what is not attracted, so the intermediate is compelled to accept a larger size. And there is no doubt that the mentioned pushing and attraction vary according to the strength and weakness of the motion. So if the motion is strong, they extend over a large distance, and if it is weak, they cover a short distance.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents the second wajh (ilzam) argument from the philosophers and the mutakallimun's response. The argument: if a body moves in a plenum, the third body (behind the second) cannot move into the second's place because it's occupied, nor into the first's place (circularity), so it must move to a fourth body's place, leading to infinite regress and motion of all bodies. The mutakallimun respond: God can annihilate the body in front of the moving body and create another in the mover's place, thus avoiding void and collision. However, the obligation is not effective against the philosophers unless rarefaction and condensation (takhalkhul and takathuf) are invalidated. The author then explains that rarefaction and condensation could allow motion without void: bodies behind rarely (increase in volume) to fill the space, and bodies in front condense (decrease in volume) to vacate space. This repels the obligation. He then elaborates with an example of motion in air: the mover pushes air in front, which pushes further air, but the push weakens until a point where air does not yield, forcing condensation (smaller volume). Similarly, air behind is attracted, weakening until a point, forcing rarefaction (larger volume). The extent of these processes depends on the force of motion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun completely reject rarefaction and condensation as impossible.
Correction: In this passage, they argue that rarefaction and condensation can account for motion in a plenum without void or collision, and it is the philosophers who must refute them.

Checkpoint

A) By the body moving at infinite speed.
B) By God annihilating the body in front and creating a new body behind.
C) By the air in front pushing back the mover.
D) By the bodies being infinitely divisible.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun's response to the second ilzam argument refocuses the debate on whether rarefaction and condensation are possible, shifting the burden to the philosophers.

?
This lesson shows two different accounts of how motion happens: divine intervention or natural processes like rarefaction and condensation. When you experience an unexpected change in your life (like a sudden illness or a new opportunity), do you instinctively attribute it to Allah's direct control or to natural causes? ?
The philosophers' argument led to an infinite regress, which the mutakallimun avoided by appealing to Allah's power. Is there an area of your life where you feel trapped in an endless cycle (like habitual sins) that you keep trying to fix on your own? Are you relying on your own 'natural' efforts instead of turning to Allah to 'annihilate' the obstacle and 'create' a new path? Objection and Answer: Rarefaction and Condensation Do Not Require Void
An objection that rarefaction and condensation require void, and the answer appealing to hyle's capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutakallimun respond to the objection that rarefaction and condensation necessitate the existence of void by appealing to the nature of hyle (hayula).

Core Idea
Rarefaction and condensation are explained by hyle's receptivity, not by void.

The existence of void (khala') was a contentious issue between the mutakallimun and the philosophers. Here, an objector argues that observable phenomena like rarefaction and condensation can only be explained by void spaces between parts. The answer rejects this premise and offers an alternative explanation rooted in the nature of hyle (hayula), the substrate of bodies. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall argument. Notice the structure: a conditional objection followed by a denial and alternative explanation.
2
Understand the objector's claim
Identify why the objector thinks rarefaction and condensation imply void: changes in volume are attributed to changes in void spaces between parts.
3
Analyze the answer's logic
The answer denies the premise and asserts that rarefaction and condensation are due to hyle's capacity to receive different magnitudes. Consider what this means: hyle has no inherent magnitude, so it can 'put on' a larger or smaller magnitude.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is this answer important? It allows the mutakallimun to explain physical phenomena without accepting void, which has theological implications regarding God's power and the nature of bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : التخلخل والتكاثف في الأجسام إنما يكونان لكثرة الخلاء وقلته فيما بين أجزاء الجسم فيكون مقداره مع كثرة الخلاء فيما بينهما كبيراً، ومع قلته صغيراً فهما يستلزمان وقوع الخلاء الذي هو المطلوب قلنا: ممنوع كونهما لما ذكرتم بل هما لأن الهيولى أمر قابل للمقدار الصغير والكبير إذ لا مقدار لها في حد نفسها ونسبتها إلى المقادير الصغيرة والكبيرة على سواء فتخلع مقداراً وتلبس مقداراً آخر أصغر أو أكبر وسيأتي ذلك فيما بعد
For it is said: Rarefaction and condensation in bodies only occur due to the abundance and scarcity of void between the parts of the body, so its magnitude becomes large with much void between them, and small with little void. Thus they necessitate the occurrence of void, which is what is sought. We say: It is denied that they are as you mentioned. Rather, they are because hyle (hayula) is a thing receptive to small and large magnitude, as it has no magnitude in itself, and its relation to small and large magnitudes is equal. So it sheds one magnitude and puts on another, smaller or larger. And this will come later.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objector argues that rarefaction and condensation (takhalkhul and takathuf) can only be explained by the increase or decrease of void spaces between the parts of a body. Thus, if a body rarely, its volume increases because there is more void between its parts; if it condenses, its volume decreases because there is less void. Therefore, rarefaction and condensation imply the existence of void (khala'), which is exactly what the mutakallimun were trying to avoid. The answer rejects this premise: rarefaction and condensation are not due to void but to the nature of hyle (hayula), which is a substrate that has no inherent magnitude and is equally receptive to any magnitude. When a body rarely, the hyle 'sheds' (takhla') its current magnitude and 'puts on' (talbas) a larger one; when it condenses, it puts on a smaller one. No void is needed. The author notes that this topic will be discussed later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun deny the reality of rarefaction and condensation.
Correction: They affirm rarefaction and condensation but explain them without void, by appealing to hyle's capacity to change magnitude.

Checkpoint

B) The capacity of hyle to receive different magnitudes.

D) The force of motion.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun reject void but explain rarefaction and condensation through hyle's capacity to change magnitude, preserving a non-void model of bodies.
